<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Sport</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Forms of competitive activity, usually physical</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Sport_(disambiguation)" title="Sport (disambiguation)">Sport (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="1918" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg/220px-London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg/330px-London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg/440px-London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:London_Marathon_2005_at_Blackfriars.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/2005_London_Marathon" title="2005 London Marathon">2005 London Marathon</a>: running races, in their various specialties, represent the oldest and most traditional form of sport.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1419" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg/300px-Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg/450px-Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg/600px-Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Youth-soccer-indiana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sport in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Childhood" title="Childhood">childhood</a>. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a>, shown above, is a <a href="/wiki/Team_sport" title="Team sport">team sport</a> which also provides opportunities to nurture <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical fitness</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_actions" title="Social actions">social interaction</a> skills.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Sport</b> pertains to any form of <a href="/wiki/Competition" title="Competition">competitive</a> <a href="/wiki/Physical_activity" title="Physical activity">physical activity</a> or <a href="/wiki/Game" title="Game">game</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportaccord_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-sportaccord-1">[1]</a></sup> that aims to use, maintain, or improve physical ability and <a href="/wiki/Skill" title="Skill">skills</a> while providing enjoyment to participants and, in some cases, <a href="/wiki/Entertainment" title="Entertainment">entertainment</a> to spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-council_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-council-2">[2]</a></sup> Sports can, through casual or organized participation, improve one's physical health. Hundreds of sports exist, from those between single contestants, through to those with hundreds of simultaneous participants, either in <a href="/wiki/Team" title="Team">teams</a> or competing as individuals. In certain sports such as <a href="/wiki/Racing" title="Racing">racing</a>, many contestants may compete, simultaneously or consecutively, with one winner; in others, the contest (a <i>match</i>) is between two sides, each attempting to exceed the other. Some sports allow a "tie" or "draw", in which there is no single winner; others provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tie-breaking_methods" title="Tie-breaking methods">tie-breaking methods</a> to ensure one winner and one loser. A number of contests may be arranged in a <a href="/wiki/Tournament" title="Tournament">tournament</a> producing a <a href="/wiki/Champion" title="Champion">champion</a>. Many <a href="/wiki/Sports_league" title="Sports league">sports leagues</a> make an annual champion by arranging games in a regular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_season" title="Sports season">sports season</a>, followed in some cases by <a href="/wiki/Playoffs" title="Playoffs">playoffs</a>.
</p><p>Sport is generally recognised as system of activities based in physical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athleticism" title="Athleticism">athleticism</a> or physical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dexterity" title="Dexterity">dexterity</a>, with major competitions such as the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> admitting only sports meeting this definition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Other organisations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, preclude activities without a physical element from classification as sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-council_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-council-2">[2]</a></sup> However, a number of competitive, but non-physical, activities claim recognition as <a href="/wiki/Mind_sport" title="Mind sport">mind sports</a>. The International Olympic Committee (through <a href="/wiki/Association_of_IOC_Recognised_International_Sports_Federations" title="Association of IOC Recognised International Sports Federations">ARISF</a>) recognises both <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contract_bridge" title="Contract bridge">bridge</a> as <i>bona fide</i> sports, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SportAccord" title="SportAccord">SportAccord</a>, the international sports federation association, recognises five non-physical sports: bridge, chess, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Draughts" title="Draughts">draughts</a> (checkers), <a href="/wiki/Go_(game)" title="Go (game)">Go</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xiangqi" title="Xiangqi">xiangqi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and limits the number of mind games which can be admitted as sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportaccord_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-sportaccord-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sport is usually governed by a set of <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_sport" title="Regulation of sport">rules</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tradition" title="Tradition">customs</a>, which serve to ensure fair competition, and allow consistent adjudication of the winner. Winning can be determined by physical events such as scoring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goal_(sport)" title="Goal (sport)">goals</a> or crossing a line first. It can also be determined by judges who are scoring elements of the sporting performance, including objective or subjective measures such as technical performance or artistic impression.
</p><p>Records of performance are often kept, and for popular sports, this information may be widely announced or reported in <a href="/wiki/Sports_journalism" title="Sports journalism">sport news</a>. Sport is also a major source of entertainment for non-participants, with <a href="/wiki/Spectator_sport" title="Spectator sport">spectator sport</a> drawing large crowds to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_venue" title="Sport venue">sport venues</a>, and reaching wider audiences through <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_of_sports_events" title="Broadcasting of sports events">broadcasting</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_betting" title="Sport betting">Sport betting</a> is in some cases severely regulated, and in some cases is central to the sport.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Kearney_(consulting_firm)" title="Kearney (consulting firm)">A.T. Kearney</a>, a consultancy, the global sporting industry is worth up to $620 billion as of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The world's most accessible and practised sport is <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> is the most popular spectator sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wa_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-wa-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meaning_and_usage">Meaning and usage</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h3>
<p>The word "<a class="external text" href="https://www.sportscouncil.in/" rel="nofollow">sport</a>" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> <i>desport</i> meaning "<a href="/wiki/Leisure" title="Leisure">leisure</a>", with the oldest definition in English from around 1300 being "anything humans find amusing or entertaining".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other meanings include gambling and events staged for the purpose of gambling; hunting; and games and diversions, including ones that require exercise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Roget's defines the noun sport as an "activity engaged in for relaxation and amusement" with synonyms including diversion and recreation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">Nomenclature</span></h3>
<p>The singular term "sport" is used in most English dialects to describe the overall concept (e.g. "children taking part in sport"), with "sports" used to describe multiple activities (e.g. "football and rugby are the most popular sports in England"). American English uses "sports" for both terms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Game#Definitions" title="Game">Game § Definitions</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChessStartingPosition.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChessStartingPosition.jpg/200px-ChessStartingPosition.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChessStartingPosition.jpg/300px-ChessStartingPosition.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChessStartingPosition.jpg/400px-ChessStartingPosition.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChessStartingPosition.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> recognises some board games as sports including <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Showjumping_white_horse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Showjumping_white_horse.jpg/200px-Showjumping_white_horse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Showjumping_white_horse.jpg/300px-Showjumping_white_horse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Showjumping_white_horse.jpg/400px-Showjumping_white_horse.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Showjumping_white_horse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Show_jumping" title="Show jumping">Show jumping</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> sport</div></div></div>
<p>The precise definition of what differentiates a sport from other leisure activities varies between sources. The closest to an international agreement on a definition is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Association_of_International_Sports_Federations" title="Global Association of International Sports Federations">Global Association of International Sports Federations</a> (GAISF), which is the association for all the largest international sports federations (including <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian sports</a>, and more), and is therefore the <i>de facto</i> representative of international sport.
</p><p>GAISF uses the following criteria, determining that a sport should:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportaccord_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-sportaccord-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>have an element of competition</li>
<li>be in no way harmful to any living creature</li>
<li>not rely on equipment provided by a single supplier (excluding proprietary games such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arena_football" title="Arena football">arena football</a>)</li>
<li>not rely on any "luck" element specifically designed into the sport.</li></ul>
<p>They also recognise that sport can be primarily physical (such as <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>), primarily mind (such as <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> or <a href="/wiki/Go_(game)" title="Go (game)">Go</a>), predominantly motorised (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formula_1" title="Formula 1">Formula 1</a> or <a href="/wiki/Powerboating" title="Powerboating">powerboating</a>), primarily co-ordination (such as <a href="/wiki/Cue_sports" title="Cue sports">billiard sports</a>), or primarily animal-supported (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equestrian_sport" title="Equestrian sport">equestrian sport</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportaccord_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-sportaccord-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>The inclusion of mind sports within sport definitions has not been universally accepted, leading to legal challenges from governing bodies in regards to being denied funding available to sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Whilst GAISF recognises a small number of mind sports, it is not open to admitting any further mind sports.
</p><p>There has been an increase in the application of the term "sport" to a wider set of non-physical challenges such as <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>, also called <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports</a> (from "electronic sports"), especially due to the large scale of participation and organised competition, but these are not widely recognised by mainstream sports organisations. According to <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, European Sports Charter, article 2.i, <span style="padding-right:.15em;">"</span>'Sport' means all forms of physical activity which, through casual or organised participation, aim at expressing or improving physical fitness and mental well-being, forming social relationships or obtaining results in competition at all levels."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="605" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg/300px-Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg/450px-Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg/600px-Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Usain_Bolt_100_m_heats_Moscow_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>100m race record holder <a href="/wiki/Usain_Bolt" title="Usain Bolt">Usain Bolt</a> (in yellow, right) and other runners, Moscow, 2013.</div></div></div>
<p>There are opposing views on the necessity of <a href="/wiki/Competition" title="Competition">competition</a> as a defining element of a sport, with almost all <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">professional sports</a> involving competition, and governing bodies requiring competition as a prerequisite of recognition by the International Olympic Committee (IOC) or GAISF. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportaccord_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-sportaccord-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other bodies advocate widening the definition of sport to include all physical activity. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> include all forms of physical exercise, including those competed just for fun.
</p><p>In order to widen participation, and reduce the impact of losing on less able participants, there has been an introduction of non-competitive physical activity to traditionally competitive events such as school <a href="/wiki/Sports_day" title="Sports day">sports days</a>, although moves like this are often controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>In competitive events, participants are graded or classified based on their "result" and often divided into groups of comparable performance, (e.g. gender, weight and age). The measurement of the result may be objective or subjective, and corrected with "handicaps" or penalties. In a race, for example, the time to complete the course is an objective measurement. In <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a> or <a href="/wiki/Diving_(sport)" title="Diving (sport)">diving</a> the result is decided by a panel of judges, and therefore subjective. There are many shades of judging between boxing and mixed martial arts, where victory is assigned by judges if neither competitor has lost at the end of the match time.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_sport" title="History of sport">History of sport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos,_2nd_century_CE_(Glyptothek_Munich).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3274" data-file-width="2030" decoding="async" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg/150px-Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg/225px-Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg/300px-Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos%2C_2nd_century_CE_%28Glyptothek_Munich%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_bronze_copy_of_Myron%E2%80%99s_Discobolos,_2nd_century_CE_(Glyptothek_Munich).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> bronze reduction of <a href="/wiki/Myron" title="Myron">Myron</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discobolos" title="Discobolos">Discobolos</a>, 2nd century AD.</div></div></div>
<p>Artifacts and structures suggest <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_China" title="Sport in China">sport in China</a> as early as 2000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Gymnastics appears to have been popular in China's ancient past. Monuments to the <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">Pharaohs</a> indicate that a number of sports, including swimming and fishing, were well-developed and regulated several thousands of years ago in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Other Egyptian sports included javelin throwing, high jump, and wrestling. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Persia" title="Ancient Persia">Ancient Persian</a> sports such as the traditional Iranian martial art of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zourkhaneh" title="Zourkhaneh">Zoorkhaneh</a> had a close connection to warfare skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Among other sports that originated in ancient Persia are <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jousting" title="Jousting">jousting</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="1522" decoding="async" height="89" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg/200px-Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg/300px-Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg/400px-Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bruno_Senna_2006_Australian_Grand_Prix.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">Motorised sports</a> have appeared since the advent of the modern age.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Participants_with_the_Water_Warrior_class_perform_squats_prior_to_entering_the_pool_at_Camp_Foster,_Okinawa,_Japan,_July_6,_2011_110706-M-VD776-004_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1736" data-file-width="2851" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Participants_with_the_Water_Warrior_class_perform_squats_prior_to_entering_the_pool_at_Camp_Foster%2C_Okinawa%2C_Japan%2C_July_6%2C_2011_110706-M-VD776-004_%28cropped%29.jpg/260px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Participants_with_the_Water_Warrior_class_perform_squats_prior_to_entering_the_pool_at_Camp_Foster%2C_Okinawa%2C_Japan%2C_July_6%2C_2011_110706-M-VD776-004_%28cropped%29.jpg/390px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Participants_with_the_Water_Warrior_class_perform_squats_prior_to_entering_the_pool_at_Camp_Foster%2C_Okinawa%2C_Japan%2C_July_6%2C_2011_110706-M-VD776-004_%28cropped%29.jpg/520px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Participants_with_the_Water_Warrior_class_perform_squats_prior_to_entering_the_pool_at_Camp_Foster,_Okinawa,_Japan,_July_6,_2011_110706-M-VD776-004_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swimmers perform <a href="/wiki/Squat_(exercise)" title="Squat (exercise)">squats</a> as <a href="/wiki/Warming_up" title="Warming up">warm-up exercise</a> prior to entering the pool in a U.S. military base, 2011</div></div></div>
<p>A wide range of sports were already established by the time of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a> and the military culture and the development of sport in Greece influenced one another considerably. Sport became such a prominent part of their culture that the Greeks created the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, which in ancient times were held every four years in a small village in the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnesus</a> called <a href="/wiki/Olympia,_Greece" title="Olympia, Greece">Olympia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sports have been increasingly organised and regulated from the time of the ancient Olympics up to the present century. Industrialisation has brought increased <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leisure_time" title="Leisure time">leisure time</a>, letting people attend and follow spectator sports and participate in athletic activities. These trends continued with the advent of <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a> and global communication. Professionalism became prevalent, further adding to the increase in sport's popularity, as sports fans followed the exploits of professional athletes – all while enjoying the exercise and competition associated with amateur participation in sports. Since the turn of the 21st century, there has been increasing debate about whether <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> sports people should be able to participate in sport events that conform with their post-transition <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fair_play">Fair play</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sportsmanship">Sportsmanship</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sportsmanship" title="Sportsmanship">Sportsmanship</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gamesmanship" title="Gamesmanship">Gamesmanship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winning_isn%27t_everything;_it%27s_the_only_thing" title="Winning isn't everything; it's the only thing">Winning isn't everything; it's the only thing</a></div>
<p>Sportsmanship is an attitude that strives for fair play, courtesy toward teammates and opponents, ethical behaviour and integrity, and grace in victory or defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sportsmanship expresses an aspiration or ethos that the activity will be enjoyed for its own sake. The well-known sentiment by sports journalist <a href="/wiki/Grantland_Rice" title="Grantland Rice">Grantland Rice</a>, that it's "not that you won or lost but how you played the game", and the modern Olympic creed expressed by its founder <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin" title="Pierre de Coubertin">Pierre de Coubertin</a>: "The most important thing... is not winning but taking part" are typical expressions of this sentiment.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cheating">Cheating</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">Match fixing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheating" title="Cheating">cheating</a></div>
<p>Key principles of sport include that the result should not be predetermined, and that both sides should have equal opportunity to win. Rules are in place to ensure fair play, but participants can break these rules in order to gain advantage.
</p><p>Participants may cheat in order to unfairly increase their chance of winning, or in order to achieve other advantages such as financial gains. The widespread existence of <a href="/wiki/Gambling" title="Gambling">gambling</a> on the results of sports fixtures creates a motivation for <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">match fixing</a>, where a participant or participants deliberately work to ensure a given outcome rather than simply playing to win.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doping_and_drugs">Doping and drugs</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Use_of_performance-enhancing_drugs_in_sport" title="Use of performance-enhancing drugs in sport">Use of performance-enhancing drugs in sport</a></div>
<p>The competitive nature of sport encourages some participants to attempt to enhance their performance through the use of medicines, or through other means such as <a href="/wiki/Blood_doping" title="Blood doping">increasing the volume of blood in their bodies through artificial means</a>.
</p><p>All sports recognised by the IOC or SportAccord are required to implement a testing programme, looking for a list of banned drugs, with suspensions or bans being placed on participants who test positive for banned substances.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence">Violence</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Violence_in_sports" title="Violence in sports">Violence in sports</a> involves crossing the line between fair competition and intentional aggressive violence. Athletes, coaches, fans, and parents sometimes unleash violent behaviour on people or property, in misguided shows of loyalty, dominance, anger, or celebration. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rioting" title="Rioting">Rioting</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hooliganism" title="Hooliganism">hooliganism</a> by fans in particular is a problem at some national and international sporting contests.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participation">Participation</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_participation">Gender participation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_(192)_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin,_3_September.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="729" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/280px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/420px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/560px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_(192)_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin,_3_September.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International level female athletes at <a href="/wiki/ISTAF_Berlin" title="ISTAF Berlin">ISTAF Berlin</a>, 2006</div></div></div>

<b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2012</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_sports" title="Women's sports">Women's sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_professional_sports" title="Women's professional sports">Women's professional sports</a></div>
<p>Female participation in sports continues to rise alongside the opportunity for involvement and the value of sports for <a href="/wiki/Child_development" title="Child development">child development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical fitness</a>. Despite increases in female participation during the last three decades, a gap persists in the enrolment figures between male and female players in sports-related teams. Female players account for 39% of the total participation in US interscholastic athletics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_participation">Youth participation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2012</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_sport" title="College sport">College sport</a></div>
<p>Youth sport presents children with opportunities for fun, socialisation, forming peer relationships, <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical fitness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Athletic_scholarship" title="Athletic scholarship">athletic scholarships</a>. Activists for <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_on_drugs" title="War on drugs">war on drugs</a> encourage youth sport as a means to increase <a href="/wiki/Participation_inequality" title="Participation inequality">educational participation</a> and to fight the <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">illegal drug trade</a>. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationwide_Children%27s_Hospital_(Columbus)#Research_and_education" title="Nationwide Children's Hospital (Columbus)">Center for Injury Research and Policy at Nationwide Children's Hospital</a>, the biggest risk for youth sport is death or serious injury including <a href="/wiki/Concussion" title="Concussion">concussion</a>. These risks come from running, basketball, association football, volleyball, gridiron, gymnastics, and ice hockey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Youth sport in the US is a $15 billion industry including equipment up to private coaching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disabled_participation">Disabled participation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2373" data-file-width="3868" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg/220px-David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg/330px-David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg/440px-David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Bizet_-_Marathon_de_Paris_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A runner gives a friendly tap on the shoulder to a wheelchair racer during the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Marathon" title="Paris Marathon"><i>Marathon International de Paris</i> (Paris Marathon)</a> in 2014.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disabled_sports" title="Disabled sports">Disabled sports</a></div>
<p><b>Disabled sports</b> also <b>adaptive sports</b> or <b>parasports</b>, are sports played by people with a <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disability</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Physical_disability" title="Physical disability">physical</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intellectual_disabilities" title="Intellectual disabilities">intellectual disabilities</a>. As many of these are based on existing sports modified to meet the needs of people with a disability, they are sometimes referred to as <i>adapted sports</i>. However, not all disabled sports are adapted; several sports that have been specifically created for people with a disability have no equivalent in able-bodied sports.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spectator_involvement">Spectator involvement</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1906_Athens_stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="638" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/1906_Athens_stadium.jpg/220px-1906_Athens_stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/1906_Athens_stadium.jpg/330px-1906_Athens_stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/1906_Athens_stadium.jpg/440px-1906_Athens_stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1906_Athens_stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spectators at the 1906 unofficial Olympic Games</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spectator_sport" title="Spectator sport">Spectator sport</a></div>
<p>The competition element of sport, along with the aesthetic appeal of some sports, result in the popularity of people attending to watch sport being played. This has led to the specific phenomenon of <a href="/wiki/Spectator_sport" title="Spectator sport">spectator sport</a>.
</p><p>Both amateur and professional sports attract spectators, both in person at the sport venue, and through broadcast media including <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">internet</a> broadcast. Both attendance in person and viewing remotely can incur a sometimes substantial charge, such as an entrance ticket, or <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> television broadcast. <a href="/wiki/Sports_league" title="Sports league">Sports league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tournament" title="Tournament">tournament</a> are two common arrangements to organize sport teams or individual athletes into competing against each other continuously or periodically.
</p><p>It is common for popular sports to attract large broadcast audiences, leading to rival broadcasters bidding large amounts of money for the rights to show certain fixtures. The football <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> attracts a global <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> audience of hundreds of millions; the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Finals" title="FIFA World Cup Finals">final</a> alone attracted an estimated worldwide audience of well over 700 million and the <a href="/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup_Final" title="2011 Cricket World Cup Final">2011 Cricket World Cup Final</a>  attracted an estimated audience of 135 million in India alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, the championship game of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>, has become one of the most watched television broadcasts of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SB15_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-SB15-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
Super Bowl Sunday is a <i>de facto</i> national holiday in America;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> the viewership being so great that in 2015, advertising space was reported as being sold at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/$" title="$">$</a>4.5m for a 30-second slot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SB15_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-SB15-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Amateur_and_professional">Amateur and professional</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volleyball-5_(9786053885).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2995" data-file-width="4500" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg/220px-Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg/330px-Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg/440px-Volleyball-5_%289786053885%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volleyball-5_(9786053885).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Women's volleyball team of a U.S. university.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_sport" title="Professional sport">Professional sport</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amateur_sport" title="Amateur sport">Amateur sport</a></div>
<p>Sport can be undertaken on an amateur, professional or semi-professional basis, depending on whether participants are incentivised for participation (usually through payment of a <a href="/wiki/Wage" title="Wage">wage</a> or <a href="/wiki/Salary" title="Salary">salary</a>). Amateur participation in sport at lower levels is often called "grassroots sport".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-council_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-council-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White_Paper_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-White_Paper-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>The popularity of <a href="/wiki/Spectator_sport" title="Spectator sport">spectator sport</a> as a recreation for non-participants has led to sport becoming a major business in its own right, and this has incentivised a high paying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_sport" title="Professional sport">professional sport</a> culture, where high performing participants are rewarded with pay far in excess of average wages, which can run into millions of dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some sports, or individual competitions within a sport, retain a policy of allowing only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amateur_sport" title="Amateur sport">amateur sport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> started with a principle of amateur competition with those who practised a sport professionally considered to have an unfair advantage over those who practised it merely as a hobby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OIdeology_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-OIdeology-32">[32]</a></sup> From 1971, Olympic athletes were allowed to receive compensation and sponsorship,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InfoPlease_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-InfoPlease-33">[33]</a></sup> and from 1986, the IOC decided to make all professional athletes eligible for the Olympics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InfoPlease_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-InfoPlease-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> with the exceptions of <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and wrestling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG/220px-Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG/330px-Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG/440px-Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Third_umpire_lights_at_Melbourne_Cricket_Ground.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>These lights at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> indicate the decision the third umpire makes following a review.</div></div></div>
<p>Technology plays an important part in modern sport. It is a necessary part of some sports (such as motorsport), and it is used in others to improve performance. Some sports also use it to allow off-field decision making.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sports_science" title="Sports science">Sports science</a> is a widespread academic discipline, and can be applied to areas including athlete performance, such as the use of video analysis to fine-tune technique, or to equipment, such as improved <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Running_shoe" title="Running shoe">running shoes</a> or <a href="/wiki/Competitive_swimwear" title="Competitive swimwear">competitive swimwear</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sports_engineering" title="Sports engineering">Sports engineering</a> emerged as a discipline in 1998 with an increasing focus not just on materials design but also the use of technology in sport, from analytics and big data to <a href="/wiki/Wearable_technology" title="Wearable technology">wearable technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaining_Steam_in_Sports_Technology_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaining_Steam_in_Sports_Technology-39">[39]</a></sup> In order to control the impact of technology on fair play, governing bodies frequently have specific rules that are set to control the impact of technical advantage between participants. For example, in 2010, full-body, non-textile swimsuits were banned by <a href="/wiki/FINA" title="FINA">FINA</a>, as they were enhancing swimmers' performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>The increase in technology has also allowed many decisions in sports matches to be taken, or reviewed, off-field, with another official using instant replays to make decisions. In some sports, players can now challenge decisions made by officials. In <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goal-line_technology" title="Goal-line technology">goal-line technology</a> makes decisions on whether a ball has crossed the goal line or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The technology is not compulsory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFABofficial_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFABofficial-43">[43]</a></sup> but was used in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA Women's World Cup">2015 FIFA Women's World Cup</a> in Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> from <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Premier_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Premier-46">[46]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> from <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Bundesliga" title="2015–16 Bundesliga">2015–16</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL" title="NFL">NFL</a>, a referee can ask for a review from the replay booth, or a head coach can issue a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Challenge_(NFL)" title="Challenge (NFL)">challenge</a> to review the play using replays. The final decision rests with the referee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> A video referee (commonly known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_match_official#Television_match_official" title="Television match official">Television Match Official</a> or TMO) can also use replays to help decision-making in rugby (both <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">union</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In international cricket, an umpire can ask the <a href="/wiki/Third_umpire" title="Third umpire">Third umpire</a> for a decision, and the third umpire makes the final decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Umpire_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Umpire-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_End_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_End-52">[52]</a></sup> Since 2008, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umpire_Decision_Review_System" title="Umpire Decision Review System">decision review system</a> for players to review decisions has been introduced and used in <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">ICC</a>-run tournaments, and optionally in other matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Umpire_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Umpire-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Depending on the host broadcaster, a number of different technologies are used during an umpire or player review, including instant replays, <a href="/wiki/Hawk-Eye" title="Hawk-Eye">Hawk-Eye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hot_Spot_(cricket)" title="Hot Spot (cricket)">Hot Spot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snickometer" title="Snickometer">Real Time Snickometer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Hawk-Eye is also used in tennis to challenge umpiring decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tind1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-tind1-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_education">Sports and education</span></h2>
<p>Research suggests that sports have the capacity to connect <a href="/wiki/Youth" title="Youth">youth</a> to positive adult role models and provide positive development opportunities, as well as promote the learning and application of life <a href="/wiki/Skill" title="Skill">skills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-59">[59]</a></sup> In recent years the use of sport to reduce <a href="/wiki/Crime" title="Crime">crime</a>, as well as to prevent <a href="/wiki/Violent_extremism" title="Violent extremism">violent extremism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radicalization" title="Radicalization">radicalization</a>, has become more widespread, especially as a tool to improve <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, enhance social bonds and provide participants with a feeling of purpose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is no high-quality evidence that shows the effectiveness of interventions to increase sports participation of the community in sports such as mass media campaigns, educational sessions, and policy changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> There is also no high-quality studies that investigate the effect of such interventions in promoting healthy behavior change in the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_and_sports" title="Politics and sports">Politics and sports</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2010</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> used the <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934 FIFA World Cup</a>, which was held in Italy, to showcase <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy#Fascist_regime_(1922–1943)" title="Kingdom of Italy">Fascist Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Fascism_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Fascism-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> also used the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1936_Winter_Olympics" title="1936 Winter Olympics">1936 Winter Olympics</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Garmisch-Partenkirchen" title="Garmisch-Partenkirchen">Garmisch-Partenkirchen</a>, to promote the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_ideology" title="Nazi ideology">Nazi ideology</a> of the superiority of the <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan race</a>, and inferiority of the Jews and other "<a href="/wiki/Untermensch" title="Untermensch">undesirables</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Fascism_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_Fascism-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sociology_Sport_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sociology_Sport-64">[64]</a></sup> Germany used the Olympics to give off a peaceful image while secretly preparing for war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> was the official policy in South Africa, many sports people, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, adopted the conscientious approach that they should not appear in competitive sports there. Some feel this was an effective contribution to the eventual demolition of the policy of apartheid, others feel that it may have prolonged and reinforced its worst effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the history of Ireland, Gaelic sports were connected with <a href="/wiki/Cultural_nationalism" title="Cultural nationalism">cultural nationalism</a>. Until the mid-20th century a person could have been banned from playing <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a>, or other sports administered by the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> (GAA) if she/he played or supported <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a>, or other games seen to be of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">British</a> origin. Until recently the GAA continued to ban the playing of football and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> at Gaelic venues. This ban, also known as Rule 42,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> is still enforced, but was modified to allow football and rugby to be played in <a href="/wiki/Croke_Park" title="Croke Park">Croke Park</a> while <a href="/wiki/Lansdowne_Road" title="Lansdowne Road">Lansdowne Road</a> was redeveloped into <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Stadium" title="Aviva Stadium">Aviva Stadium</a>. Until recently, under Rule 21, the GAA also banned members of the British security forces and members of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">RUC</a> from playing Gaelic games, but the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998 led to the eventual removal of the ban.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">Nationalism</a> is often evident in the pursuit of sport, or in its reporting: people compete in national teams, or commentators and audiences can adopt a partisan view. On occasion, such tensions can lead to violent confrontation among players or spectators within and beyond the sporting venue, as in the <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">Football War</a>. These trends are seen by many as contrary to the fundamental ethos of sport being carried on for its own sake and for the enjoyment of its participants.
</p><p>Sport and politics collided in the 1972 Olympics in Munich. Masked men entered the hotel of the Israeli Olympic team and killed many of their men. This was known as the <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a>.
</p><p>A study of US elections has shown that the result of sports events can affect the results. A study published in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proceedings_of_the_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences</a> showed that when the home team wins the game before the election, the incumbent candidates can increase their share of the vote by 1.5 percent. A loss had the opposite effect, and the effect is greater for higher-profile teams or unexpected wins and losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Also, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Washington Redskins</a> win their final game before an election, then the incumbent President is more likely to win, and if the Redskins lose, then the opposition candidate is more likely to win; this has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Redskins_Rule" title="Redskins Rule">Redskins Rule</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_means_of_controlling_and_subduing_populations">As a means of controlling and subduing populations</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_de_La_Bo%C3%A9tie" title="Étienne de La Boétie">Étienne de La Boétie</a>, in his essay <i><a href="/wiki/Discourse_on_Voluntary_Servitude" title="Discourse on Voluntary Servitude">Discourse on Voluntary Servitude</a></i> describes athletic spectacles as means for tyrants to control their subjects by distracting them.
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Do not imagine that there is any bird more easily caught by decoy, nor any fish sooner fixed on the hook by wormy bait, than are all these poor fools neatly tricked into servitude by the slightest feather passed, so to speak, before their mouths. Truly it is a marvellous thing that they let themselves be caught so quickly at the slightest tickling of their fancy. Plays, farces, spectacles, gladiators, strange beasts, medals, pictures, and other such opiates, these were for ancient peoples the bait toward slavery, the price of their liberty, the instruments of tyranny. By these practices and enticements the ancient dictators so successfully lulled their subjects under the yoke, that the stupefied peoples, fascinated by the pastimes and vain pleasures flashed before their eyes, learned subservience as naïvely, but not so creditably, as little children learn to read by looking at bright picture books.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3275" data-file-width="2470" decoding="async" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg/220px-Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg/330px-Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg/440px-Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panathenaic_amphora_Kleophrades_Louvre_F277.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The foot race was one of the events dedicated to Zeus. Panathenaic amphora, Kleophrades painter, circa 500 BC, Louvre museum.</div></div></div>
<p>Sport was an important form of worship in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_religion" title="Ancient Greek religion">Ancient Greek religion</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Olympic_Games" title="Ancient Olympic Games">ancient Olympic Games</a> were held in honour of the head deity, <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a>, and featured various forms of religious dedication to him and other gods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> As many Greeks travelled to see the games, this combination of religion and sport also served as a way of uniting them.
</p><p>The practice of athletic competitions has been criticised by some Christian thinkers as a form of <a href="/wiki/Idolatry" title="Idolatry">idolatry</a>, in which "human beings extol themselves, adore themselves, sacrifice themselves and reward themselves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson1_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Watson1-73">[73]</a></sup> Sports are seen by these critics as a manifestation of "collective pride" and "national self-deification" in which feats of human power are idolized at the expense of divine worship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson1_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Watson1-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tertullian" title="Tertullian">Tertullian</a> condemns the athletic performances of his day, insisting "the entire apparatus of the shows is based upon idolatry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The shows, says Tertullian, excite passions foreign to the calm temperament cultivated by the Christian:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>God has enjoined us to deal calmly, gently, quietly, and peacefully with the Holy Spirit, because these things are alone in keeping with the goodness of His nature, with His tenderness and sensitiveness. ... Well, how shall this be made to accord with the shows? For the show always leads to spiritual agitation, since where there is pleasure, there is keenness of feeling giving pleasure its zest; and where there is keenness of feeling, there is rivalry giving in turn its zest to that. Then, too, where you have rivalry, you have rage, bitterness, wrath and grief, with all bad things which flow from them – the whole entirely out of keeping with the religion of Christ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Christian clerics in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wesleyan-Holiness_movement" title="Wesleyan-Holiness movement">Wesleyan-Holiness movement</a> oppose the viewing of or participation in professional sports, believing that professional sports leagues <a href="/wiki/Sabbath_desecration" title="Sabbath desecration">profane the Sabbath</a> as in the modern era, certain associations hold games on the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Day" title="Lord's Day">Lord's Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handel2020_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Handel2020-76">[76]</a></sup> They also criticize professional sports for its fostering of a commitment that competes with a Christian's primary commitment to God in opposition to <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/1_Corinthians#7:35" title="s:Bible (King James)/1 Corinthians">1 Corinthians 7:35</a>, what they perceive to be a lack of modesty in the players' and cheerleaders' uniforms (which are not in conformity with the Methodistic doctrine of outward holiness), its association with violence in opposition to <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Hebrews#7:26" title="s:Bible (King James)/Hebrews">Hebrews 7:26</a>, what they perceive to be the extensive use of profanity among many players that contravenes <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/Colossians#3:8" title="s:Bible (King James)/Colossians">Colossians 3:8–10</a>, and the frequent presence of gambling, as well as alcohol and other drugs at sporting events, which go against a commitment to <a href="/wiki/Teetotalism" title="Teetotalism">teetotalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handel2020_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Handel2020-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span></h2>
